Contributor Pain Points & Ideas
https://github.com/SoftwareEngineeringDaily/software-engineering-daily-api/issues/251
Unsolved
This is a discussion issue where we are inviting all contributors (existing and potential) to bring forth Software Daily Project pain points as well as ideas to address them. These can apply to any of the repos but I've created it here as this is the most active repo.
Pain points are anything that creates friction in your ability to contribute to the Project. It could mostly affect part time volunteers, core maintainers, or both. After some time we can put together a plan to implement solutions to the most significant or common pain points.

Better and more consistent approach to env config
https://github.com/SoftwareEngineeringDaily/software-engineering-daily-api/issues/238
Unsolved
As referenced in #231 - there are too many items in /config/config.js that are required env variables but only really relevant to production, (maybe) staging, and for specific devs working on those features. These are those related to external services - Stripe, Mail Chimp, etc. They're not relevant to CI and for most devs doing core app work.
I also noticed when starting to look at this that we are not fully consistent in how we many env variables. For example, MAILCHIMP_KEY is defined and accessed via /config/config.js while STRIPE_PUBLIC_KEY is accessed via process.env - so there may be an opportunity to be a bit more consistent.
Before putting in a PR - was looking for some input on best option to organize from @jasonify and @andrewmarklloyd. @abdulbasitkay - your input would also be appreciated and I'm pretty sure this is relevant to the work related to Cloud9 you're starting to look into.
Define everything through /config/config.js. Make external service variables optional (MAILCHIMP_KEY, etc).
Strip down /config/config.js to only those items that are core to the app, for external services use process.env (what we are already doing with Stripe and AWS)
My preference is option 1 as it would be more explicit and overall more consistent but I'm open to either. For option 1 in Joi we can make the optional items simple optional() or use a fake key default like default('mailchimp_key-us6'). I think the later would be best.
I'm also not sure why we have a separate .env.docker_example. I think this and .env.local_example can be removed and we can just use a .env.example.
joshmorel opened this issue on 15 May ¬∑ 5 comments

Add better error reporting to event stream
https://github.com/SoftwareEngineeringDaily/software-engineering-daily-api/issues/225
Unsolved
@tyler-furby @abdulbasitkay @jasonify @joshmorel I'm looking into better error reporting for the API. Currently it's up to each controller (or any class) to use the sendError helper. Here's an example usage. What if instead we abstracted it to the APIError.js class itself? So instead of every time a class creates the APIError and has to also use the sendError helper, what if the APIError just sent the error to the event stream instead?

Listener Data Management
https://github.com/SoftwareEngineeringDaily/software-engineering-daily-api/issues/221
Unsolved
We need an API for getting a user's listened history. I'm not sure where the listen data is stored (InfluxDB, Firebase?) but it is definitely not easily accessible.
Once we have that API, it will be much easier to build:
a custom recommendation system (we should probably replace our Raccoon powered one eventually)
the ability to serve related links to people
other collaborative filtering related features (connecting users who listen to similar material)
Opening up a discussion for how to tackle this problem.

List is very US-centric
https://github.com/j-delaney/easy-application/issues/129
Unsolved
I count just 11 companies out of the 382 listed that have offices in the UK (bias: I live there), 21 offer remote working arrangements. Not all programmers live in California, you know ;)

This also instantly helps people narrow down their choices to countries they can easily obtain right to work in (ie. EU nationals can move to another EU country (exception: countries that shot themselves in the foot, like the UK) and just start work there, but moving to California requires a green card or H1B (is that what it's called?)).

Libmjollnir should compute the dominator tree
https://github.com/thorkill/eresi/issues/101
Unsolved
A requirement for optimal translation into SSA form is to compute the dominator tree of the control flow graph.
There are many algorithms to compute that tree. An example is following the algorithm of the "Program Structure Tree". Another is fix-point based and described on the wikipedia page for the dominator tree.

ERESI should be able to type functions
https://github.com/thorkill/eresi/issues/99
Unsolved
The ERESI type system is currently unable to give types to functions. Such feature would allow us to:
Give a type to ERESI commands and functions and be able to type-check them.
Define more-high level function-based constructs for static analysis (ex: fixed-point computations)
Enhance reflections of the ERESI environment by typing internal functions in the ERESI type system

readmema and writemem handlers should check input address mapping
https://github.com/thorkill/eresi/issues/93
Unsolved
The vectors "readmema" and "writemem" will in certain conditions read or write to an invalid address, leading to a segmentation fault when in e2dbg. Other programs seems immune against this error, so only elfsh_get_raw_by_addr() seem to be affected.
Many commands seems to be affected by that bug, D, X, write in particular.
In practice, for example:
The "write" command, when in debug mode, will not check if the address provided is really mapped. It will directly write to it. Its not straightforward to do that test, but I can think of 2 solutions:
look in the linkmap if the addr is part of a mapped object (but the stack and the heap are maybe not part of the linkmap ? to verify...)
handle the SIGSEGV and print "address not mapped" in the handler, so we could report the problem and continue the execution as if nothing had happened, obviously without doing the write.

Deploy to latest 3.6
https://github.com/UCL/rsd-engineeringcourse/issues/127
Unsolved
In order to deploy to the latest package versions on 3.6 I have done the following:
add nbformat to requirements.txt
edit merge.py as follows:
from nbformat import read as nb_read
from nbformat import writes as nb_write
... 
nb = nb_read(f, as_version=4)
... 
result = nb_write(merged)
edit .travis.yml to:
- gem install liquid -v 4.0.0
- gem install jekyll -v 3.8.4
Hope this helps.
Giovanni1085 opened this issue on 2 Oct ¬∑ 0 comments

Only allow specific errors in notebooks
https://github.com/UCL/rsd-engineeringcourse/issues/121
Unsolved
Some of the notebooks contain cells that intentionally cause errors, which breaks the execution. We are currently running nbconvert --allow-errors to continue the conversion after an error occurs, but this means we are potentially letting other errors through without noticing (there doesn't seem to be a way to get all the errors raised).
Version 5.4 of nbconvert has support for the raises-exception tag, which lets you specify that a particular cell is expected to produce an error, and shouldn't stop the conversion if an exception is raised (there is an issue open for the inverse, requiring that the cell produces the error, and stopping the conversion if it doesn't). If we use that, then we should be able to just run nbconvert and only accept the errors we have put there intentionally.

Add content to "Management 3.0"
https://github.com/stevenschwenke/SoftwareEngineeringCourse/issues/8
Unsolved
Source: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dgKKPQiRRag&feature=youtu.be
study by MIT: gave students different tasks to do, reward them with money according to their performance: Good performance -> more money
as long as task only mechanical, no-brain-activity: more money led to more performance
cognitive tasks: more money led to LESS performance
other studies show: people above a certain level of skill work different then those below
no "if this then that"-logic
"pay people enough so they think about work, not money. Then give them responsibility and autonomy to get best results"
"you problably want to do something interesting, so let me get out of your way" should be the way management works
main motivations for open source contributors: challenge, mastery, making a contribution
=> organizations need a purpose to get the good guys => see mission statements of companies

upvote/downvote score display is confusing/inconsistent
https://github.com/SoftwareEngineeringDaily/sedaily-front-end/issues/535
Unsolved
I came across this while trying to finish the manual testing checklist with Cypress e2e tests. I do recall discussing in Slack that the default of 1 score was a bit confusing but let it be as. The problem here is that it is also inconsistent. The displayed score will drop from 1 to -1 when the backend score drops from -1 to -2.
This has to do with the JS expression in src/components/VotingArrows.vue: <div class='score-text'>{{ score + 1 || 1}}</div>. If score = -1, score + 1 is 0 or falsy so it will display 1. But if it's -1 it's truthy so will display -1.
Based on how the app is use this is super low priority but I'm going to test the voting different in Cypress until the expected behaviour is clarified. @tyler-furby - What was the original intent around this change?

Error in pixel_spec.rb
https://github.com/Bloc/sep-assignments/issues/128
Unsolved
Looks like there was a mistake in pixel_spec.rb
    it "corrects a blue value if it's less than 0" do
      pixel = Pixel.new(100, -10, 100, 5, 5)
      expect(pixel.green).to eq 0
    end
    
    it "corrects a green value if it's less than 0" do
      pixel = Pixel.new(100, 100, -12, 5, 5)
      expect(pixel.blue).to eq 0
    end
You are checking the wrong values for the green and blue specs.

Review template
Before filling in this review, please read our Advice to Reviewers.
(If you have confidential comments about this chapter, please email them to one of the book editors.)
Title of chapter
Are your Post-release Defects Post-al? (or: How the Release Process Impacts your Software Analytics)
URL to the chapter
_the markdown file. e.g. https://github.com/ds4se/chapters/blob/master/zimmermann/card-sorting.md _
https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ds4se/chapters/3d0def9cc5d06423c55a0e52d4e2636b9f53fa7d/bramadams/releng.md
Message?
What is the chapter's clear and approachable take away message?
Researchers should match defect reports with code changes with the releases in their predictive analytics (defect prediction) models.
Accessible?
Is the chapters written for a generalist audience (no excessive use of technical terminology) with a minimum of diagrams and references? How can it be made more accessible to generalist?
The authors use lots of terms such as trunk, version control system, post release defects that may not be understood by a generalist. They may consider starting the paper with an example that would make it easier to understand by a general audience.
Size?
Is the chapter the right length? Should anything missing be added? Can anything superfluous be removed (e.g. by deleting some section that does not work so well or by using less jargon, less formulae, lees diagrams, less references).? What are the aspects of the chapter that authors SHOULD change?
The size of the chapter is right.
Gotta Mantra?
We encouraged (but did not require) the chapter title to be a mantra or something cute/catchy, i.e., some slogan reflecting best practice for data science for SE? If you have suggestion for a better title, please put them here.
The current title suggests to get take-home message from the paper, however the authors really discuss the impact of release process in software analytics, therefore they may consider an alternative title: ‚ÄúHow the Release Process Impacts your Software Analytics‚Äù
Best Points
What are the best points of the chapter that the authors should NOT change?
The initial student-professor dialogue is nice.
The message is good.

Review of "Open from the Beginning" by Earl Barr
https://github.com/ds4se/chapters/issues/123
Unsolved
Review
Title of chapter
Open from the Beginning
URL to the chapter
https://github.com/ds4se/chapters/tree/master/gousiosg/open-from-the-beginning.md
Message?
What is the chapter's clear and approachable take away message?
Just like research papers, data and tooling should be open from the beginning.
Accessible?
This paper is accessible to the generalist.
Size?
This chapter is the right length.
What are the aspects of the chapter that authors SHOULD change?
I, for one, would be interested in reading more technical details about Alitheia and GHTorrent. I am curious to see if I agree with Georgios contention that openness per se is the main reason for the uptake of GHTorrent. Perhaps the tooling used to build GHTorrent is more popular? Georgios writes that GHTorrent grew with its users: this observation would be strengthened if he stated how many external patches, if any, he accepted.
How does GHTorrent compare to Boa?
Copyedits
"We do not show the same jealousy with the artifacts that comprise our research"
Jealousy is inappropriate here. I suggest:
"We are not so zealous with the artifacts..."
"of making our research even more widespread."
A more idiomatic way to phrase this is "of increasing the impact of our research."
"My PhD supervisor,"
Lose the comma:
"My PhD supervisor"
hacky Shell -> hacky shell
"The work is messy and often confuses the reader in terms of what have they done and how they have done."
This quote is agrammatical: the verb to do is transitive and therefore requires an object. Perhaps the actual quote ends with "and who they have done it."? If the actual quote is erroneous, Georgios should consider adding [sic] to signal that the error is in the original quote.
"The experiment seems foley, results somewhat lacking"
'Foley' is not an English word.
The titles are not in title case.
Gotta Mantra?
This chapter is already well-titled.
Best Points
What are the best points of the chapter that the authors should NOT change?
Georgios has built this chapter on two examples which he compares and contrasts. This is an effective rhetorical device that he should retain.
barr opened this issue on 21 Dec 2015 ¬∑ 1 comment

Review of ./muench/Chapter_Muench.md

Unsolved
Best Points
The chapter provides a good overview of the book and why compiling a book on data science in software context is important. If this chapter is to serve the overview of the entire book, I hope it includes a table of content.
Title of chapter
Learning Lessons over Lessons Learnt: Liftoff with Continuous Experimentation Towards Rapid Value Delivery
URL to the chapter
https://github.com/ds4se/chapters/blob/master/muench/Chapter_Muench.md

The problem of testing the value of features early on is well motivated by the chapter. The chapter is engaging to read and the message is very clear. "usually good in" => "usually good at"

Best Points

Review for Mining Mobile App Stores
https://github.com/ds4se/chapters/issues/117
Unsolved
This was a fun chapter to read, but it suffers from three minor-to-moderate problems that, if addressed, would improve the chapter in my view.
MODERATE: The chapter is descriptive and clear in the treatment of the problem but does not contain actionable advice. What can I, either as a developer or user of mobile apps, do (better) as a result of the described mining exercise and subsequent analysis?
MODERATE: The chapter does not have a thesis statement up front nor a conclusion at the end. I found the last paragraph, which listed other things one could do with app repositories, distracting and out of place. I was expecting a punchline there. Along with the lack of actionable advice (issue #1), this made it look like more support for mining ‚Äúbecause we can‚Äù.
MINOR: The following sentence struck me as a tautology: ‚ÄúFor example, a 1 to 2 star ratio of 5 for a complaint type indicates that this complaint type has 5 times as many 1 star ratings as 2 star ratings.‚Äù I think it can easily be removed without loss of understandability or content. I think it would also be interesting to see, if you have the data, to what extent developers respond to the really negative comments in subsequent releases, and whether this, in turn, improves the given app‚Äôs reviews.

I have only few comments: (1) The alternative title does not seem completely aligned with the chapter content as the whole chapter deals with defects models and not in general with software analytics. I would drop it or maybe compound the two titles into something like ‚ÄúHow the Release Process Impacts on Defect Prediction Modeling‚Äù; (2) The paragraph at the end of the first section sounds a bit academic. I would anticipate it soon after the student‚Äôs case and rephrase it a bit explaining what is in general the problem in analyzing defect data across releases. Perhaps just removing the sentence ‚ÄúThe following sections discuss how steps (1) and (2) can go wrong when the release process of a project is not taken into account, and what could be done to resolve these problems.‚Äù and rephrasing the second sentence can be enough. (3) I would suggest saying explicitly ‚Äúfile-level defect prediction model‚Äù (i.e., removing the brackets around ‚Äúfile-level‚Äù) as there are other defect prediction models that do not use file characteristics. (e.g., Lyu‚Äôs models). In fact releases can impact on other types of defect models too. Maybe I it would be good to stress that the file-level defect models are one example which releases have impact on.
Gotta Mantra?
We encouraged (but did not require) the chapter title to be a mantra or something cute/catchy, i.e., some slogan reflecting best practice for data science for SE? If you have suggestion for a better title, please put them here.
More than a mantra, I would suggest to align the title with the content of the chapter. For example ‚ÄúHow the Release Process Impacts on Defect Prediction Modeling‚Äù
Best Points
What are the best points of the chapter that the authors should NOT change?
The student case and the last section ‚ÄúHow the Version Control System can Help.‚Äù
brusso123 opened this issue on 17 Nov 2015 ¬∑ 0 comments

Title of chapter

Message?
The authors' visual analytics tool, MetroEyes, can help people who are not data scientists to analyze software engineering data.
Accessible?

Size?

Should anything missing be added?

No

Contradiction concerning PATCH HTTP status code
https://github.com/deliveroo/deliveroo.engineering/issues/135
Unsolved
It seems there's a contradiction in the guidelines concerning HTTP status codes return by PATCH:
In PATCH, mutating entities
200 OK, if the modification succeeded
In Return codes and errors
POST and PATCH should never result in a 200 (generally 201, occasionally 202).
arno-di-loreto opened this issue on 23 Apr 2017 ¬∑ 0 comments

Gently "enforce" whitespace removal and common code formatting rules in guidelines source
https://github.com/deliveroo/deliveroo.engineering/issues/122
Unsolved
Why?
To minimize annoying diffs and potential conflicts due to whitespace and code formatting in general.
A recent example of the problem is #121 in which I've made a simple change (literally added a -).
Because of my editor setup to remove whitespace at the end of the line, there where changes in irrelevant lines.
Possible solution
We could use something like http://editorconfig.org/ to (try to) "enforce" it in non-critical repositories/projects such as this one.
Like, including a .editorconfig in the project root.
This way we will be lowering the barrier because most of the editors/IDEs has support for that.
The side effects will be minimal for everyone NOT using .editorconfig. It does not break anything.
Also if anyone wants to (s)he can download a plugin from http://editorconfig.org/#download
Help wanted
What do you guys think? Should we go for it?
xarisd opened this issue on 15 Feb 2017 ¬∑ 5 comments

Expand on API guidelines: versioning
https://github.com/deliveroo/deliveroo.engineering/issues/30
Unsolved
@tompave-roo suggested in #23 that we expand on API guidelines:
Can we be a bit more specific about what we intend with "API versioning"?
And, should API versions be endpoint specific?
Common questions I've heard asked in the past:
are API versions relative to specific paths, or to the entire API surface?
in other words can a v=2 be released only for some paths?
if a new version must be rolled out for the same API, is it ok to have /dogs v2 and /dogs v1 return different responses, but /cats v2 be a simple alias for /cats v1?
what about cases where the resource sets of different versions are different? For example, /koalas might be introduced with v=3.
Some of these might be misconceptions of how API versioning works, but then it would be a good idea to state clearly how this should work.
mezis opened this issue on 26 Aug 2016 ¬∑ 0 comments

simaos opened this issue on 10 Jul ¬∑ 0 comments

Docker overview - add app packaging & OS config automation analogies
https://github.com/uribench/software-engineering-handbook/issues/9
Unsolved
Docker overviews sometimes focus on the top-down description with analogies to Docker being a lightweight VM or similar. A bottom-up context is, instead, an analogy with application dependency packaging & installers. For example, walking through: create a component->add dependent components to create a package->add external library dependencies->add OS config dependencies, e.g., FS directories, other apps->package all of these into an installer (sometimes with OS config automation, e.g., puppet/chef/ansible/salt). You can then think of a container as an alternative to an installer/OS config automation. It packages all dependencies together including some OS config dependencies -- the container is like a post-install/post-config packaging of the application.
simaos opened this issue on 10 Jul ¬∑ 0 comments

Consider adding CI tests
https://github.com/uribench/software-engineering-handbook/issues/8
Unsolved
It would probably be beneficial if the repo runs automated build tests on each PR and each push.
Things that can be tested:
Markdown style - can be done with markdownlint (ruby) or pymarkdownliny (python)
Broken links - can be done with markdown-helpers (ruby)
Config folder validation (custom solution)
There are two implementation routes as I see them:
Implement all the code needed for testing in this repo directly. This is easier, but probably less desirable, if we want to keep the repo's "documentation only" nature.
Implement all the code needed as part of the software-engineering-handbook-tools repo - but then, it must first be converted to an installable pip package, so it is accessible to Travis.
DannyBen opened this issue on 4 Jul ¬∑ 0 comments

Run automatic build of the Handbook folder
https://github.com/uribench/software-engineering-handbook/issues/6
Unsolved
Call 'handbook build' command automatically to always keep the Handbook folder on the GitHub repository current with the contents (guides and topics) and config files.
Suggested by @richardapeters to eliminate conflicts between different contributions in which one contributor is building the handbook with contents of another contributor that did not build the handbook.
This automation can be done at various points along the pipeline from the 'git commit' to the local clone until the pull request on GitHub.

Inserting new code above existing code temporarily shifts adorners
https://github.com/ermau/Instant/issues/22
Unsolved
int x = 5;  [x | 5]
int y = 2   [x | 5]
int x = 5;
Once you add the = 2, Roslyn sees the line as a 'valid' variable declarator, despite the lack of semicolon. Since it won't actually compile, it won't get executed and therefore there's a disparity between current and last executed operation IDs.
ermau opened this issue on 30 Sep 2012 ¬∑ 0 comments

Object snapshots
https://github.com/ermau/Instant/issues/21
Unsolved
Currently, object values are simply strings generated by [DebuggerDisplay] and/or .ToString(); We need to be able to take a snapshot of the object's state if we ever want to be able to move closer to debugger-like functionality.
We could:
Create a deep copy of the object (hard, slow, complete)
Track external property changes differently, associating it with the object (easy, faster, far from complete)
This would probably be an optional feature, given potential performance implications.
ermau opened this issue on 23 Sep 2012 ¬∑ 1 comment

Unsolved

Also, allow users to optionally wait for these external calls to finish once (and be cached) if they initially time out.

Mobile Element finding crashes when contigs are identified across two IS elements
https://github.com/churchlab/millstone/issues/675
Unsolved
Mobile element calling code contains an assertion that both sets of vertices come from the same mobile element. We have found cases where this fails:
# in genome_finish/graph_contig_placement.py
>translocation_seq_verts
[ME_insertion_sequence:IS150_RC_121, ME_insertion_sequence:IS186_RC_253]
This could be because the mobile elements look similar at the alignment region.
There are two ways to fix this:
ignore these mobile elements (not ideal)
combine them with (IS150/IS186)
I think this is just a really confusing highly paralogous region. I blasted the contig and just got more confused. However, there is definitely an IS element involved here:

Comprehension chapter confusion
https://github.com/andyjko/cooperative-software-development/issues/35
Unsolved
Wow, a large fraction of students bombed the reading quiz for 5.2 (Comprehension). They did not get the meaning of consistency or static typing. They were thrown off by the sentence that said that React JS used a declarative programming paradigm, making it easier to debug, and inferred that it must mean that JS also uses a declarative paradigm. Oops. I think this may correlate with general programming experiences among the students in the class.
andyjko opened this issue on 20 Jun ¬∑ 0 comments

Add accessibility module
https://github.com/andyjko/cooperative-software-development/issues/34
Unsolved
Anushka's feedback:
Hi! I think it went really well. We covered a lot of ground with an overview of accessibility development and then a deep dive into autism. I included two brainstorming breakouts with their teams. They identified some problem areas with their current apps (e.g., lack of keyboard support, inaccessible graphics). I talked about the semantic web & that seemed like new info to everyone. We had a good discussion about the nuances of designing for a user group like autism. A student even brought up the juicy question of whether we should design an app that's accessible for everyone or tailor experiences based on user profiles. I think there's value in having this type of accessibility-focused module in the course going forward. Or incorporating accessibility principles in the other modules. What are your thoughts on that?
andyjko opened this issue on 31 May ¬∑ 0 comments

Misleading dates on PL years
https://github.com/andyjko/cooperative-software-development/issues/33
Unsolved
From Shriram Krishnamurthi:
Fortran wasn't invented in 2002, Lisp in 1978, etc. In fact, the Fortran, C++ and Smalltalk references would suggest that all three languages are younger than the three languages at the end of the sentence: Java, Python, and JavaScript! I think you should model better scholarship for your students. In particular, citing a person who did not create Fortran for Fortran is ‚Ä¶ wrong (at least the other three credit their creators).

Conways law is confusing
https://github.com/andyjko/cooperative-software-development/issues/26
Unsolved
From Andy Begel:
The Communication reading does a poor job of explaining Conway‚Äôs Law. Most students who answered the ‚ÄúWhat is Conway‚Äôs Law‚Äù reading quiz seem to think it says that the application reflects the values of the teams of people who built it; that is, if people can work together well, then the product will turn out ok. Maybe that‚Äôs a corollary, but it misses the simpler point of the communication structures mirroring the organizational hierarchy.

Do not use absolute URLS to rse.shef.ac.uk
https://github.com/RSE-Sheffield/RSE-Sheffield.github.io/issues/102
Unsolved
In several pages and posts there are absolute links to https://rse.shef.ac.uk.
These do not work in local builds, and if we were to change the root of the site all these URLS would need updating. Nikola provides a mechanism to link directly to individual posts or tags (see https://getnikola.com/path-handlers.html) although the root path handler does not behave as expected, so I'm unsure of the most nikola-correct way of linking to a page such as https://rse.shef.ac.uk/contact/alumni.

Replace the regex expression to remove all string/character and comments of failing test methods
https://github.com/rjust/defects4j/issues/185
Unsolved
The framework/util/rm_broken_tests.pl script parses the output of a test suite compilation/execution and fixes failing test methods by replacing each broken test method with a dummy test method in the source file of the corresponding test class. For instance, supposing the following test suite with a failing test method (test1):
public class TestFoo {
  @Test
  public void test0() {
    assertTrue(true);
  }

  @Test
  public void test1() {
    String str = new String();
    str = 123456789;
  }
}
is then transformed to:
public class TestFoo {
  @Test
  public void test0() {
    assertTrue(true);
  }

  @Test
  public void test1() {}
// Defects4J: flaky method
//   @Test
//   public void test1() {
//     String str = new String();
//     str = 123456789;
//   }
}
Basically, the script parses the compilation/execution output and identifies the line where the failing test method starts/ends and it uses a regex expression to remove all string/character and comments of the failing test method as they may contain unbalanced delimiters or brackets (which may cause problems to find the last } of the test method). Although the script has been working fine in general, two issues (#96 and #184) have been reported related to that regex expression. Perhaps a more robust solution would be to build a parser that computes a line-number table for all methods and then use that table to comment out failing test methods.

TravisCI builds fail nondeterministically
https://github.com/rjust/defects4j/issues/172
Unsolved
Currently, there are four factors in the TravisCI process that can cause a nondeterministic failure, rather than a failure that comes as the result of any changes made to the Defects4J framework. Three of these are clearly related to timing issues that seem to occur on TravisCI - likely as a result of how TravisCI allocated virtual machines.
Potentially helpful information here: https://docs.travis-ci.com/user/reference/overview/
Issue 1:
Jobs time out after 50 minutes. This can happen to any task, even if it completed successfully in a previous build - the time needed to complete a task is not consistent. The best solution may be to split some tasks into a larger number. However, at times, any task in the list can time out.
Issue 2:
TravisCI job 2 (carton exec ./test_mutation_analysis.sh) sometimes fails nondeterministically. 36 mutants are supposed to be killed by the test, but at times, an additional 37th mutant is killed.
$ carton exec ./test_mutation_analysis.sh
Check out cff0f1ae to /tmp/test_d4j/Lang-6f................................ OK
Init local repository...................................................... OK
Tag post-fix revision...................................................... OK
Initialize fixed program version........................................... OK
Apply patch................................................................ OK
Initialize buggy program version........................................... OK
Diff cff0f1ae:6823c374..................................................... OK
Apply patch................................................................ OK
Tag pre-fix revision....................................................... OK
Check out program version: Lang-6f......................................... OK
Compiling mutant definition (mml).......................................... OK
Running ant (mutate)....................................................... OK
Running ant (compile.tests)................................................ OK
Running ant (mutation.test)................................................ OK
Mutants generated: 42
Mutants covered: 42
Mutants killed: 37
Mutation score: 88.1% (88.1%)
Total run time: 7.9 seconds
Error: Unexpected number of mutants killed (expected: 36, actual: 37)!
================================================================================
FAILED
Issue 3:
Task 43 (carton exec ./test_verify_bugs.sh -p Math -b1..18) fails nondeterministically.
One of the relevant tests for Math 15 (org.apache.commons.math3.genetics.FixedElapsedTimeTest::testIsSatisfied) is based on timing constraints and fails on TravisCI nondeterministically. I cannot replicate this issue locally, so I suspect it is related to TravisCI VM allocation.
Issue 4:
Tasks 48-50:
carton exec ./test_verify_bugs.sh -p Mockito -b1..5
carton exec ./test_verify_bugs.sh -p Mockito -b6..10
script: carton exec ./test_verify_bugs.sh -p Mockito -b11..15
One of the relevant tests for Mockito versions 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 9, 10, and 11 (org.mockitousage.verification.VerificationAfterDelayTest::shouldVerifyNormallyWithSpecificTimes) is based on timing constraints and fails on TravisCI nondeterministically. I cannot replicate this issue locally, so I suspect it is related to TravisCI VM allocation.
Note that in both this case and the Math case, the flaky tests could be removed without issue. They are not trigger tests. They are on the relevant test list because they load affected classes, but are not used to verify behavior relevant to the noted issues.
Greg4cr opened this issue on 17 Aug ¬∑ 0 comments

Create glossary of terms in readme
https://github.com/rjust/defects4j/issues/123
Unsolved
commit-db : csv table for storage of issues we can use
PID : project id
BID : bug id, sometimes used interchangeably with vid but usually just a number.
work_dir : local directory to work out of
vid : version id, "${vid}b" for buggy and "${vid}f" for fixed; it is worth noting, numerically higher vids are older than lower vids
Vcs : version control system (be it git, mecurial or subversion or other, all inherit from Vcs.pm)
revision_id : a Vcs revision id
SCRIPT_DIR: ~Defects4J_root/framework/core

Research Report by zhan0850
https://github.com/gardners/2014SE3/issues/251
Unsolved
Software Testing - Role, Principles, and Limitations
1.Introduction
The following definition of software testing is cited from a conference material written by Cem Kaner, 2006, and is quoted by Wikipedia as a widely-accepted definition:
"Software testing is an investigation conducted to provide stakeholders with information about the quality of the product or service under test." [1]
The statement classifies testing as an investigation that shows stakeholders
how good the quality of the software under development is. It gives the idea that testing is important to the product software. It does not contain information about how the investigation should be performed and to what extent developers can rely on testing.
As an expansion to the above, this report first analyses the role of testing in software development process, then introduces some rules of thumbs to apply general testing techniques, and finally discusses what testing is not and what cannot be achieved through testing.
2.The Role of Testing in Software Development
The importance of testing in a software development process is necessary to be understood by every software engineer, but is also trivial. Testing does not only reduce number of bugs in codes, it also examines if the implemented functionalities meet the corresponding requirements.
2.1 Testing in Waterfall Model
In a traditional waterfall model, testing is the one last step before the product system is delivered to customer. All assessments about meeting the requirements are carried out at this stage. However, with very limited time allowed for the entire project, it is very often that the time remaining for testing is squeezed heavily.
Moreover, In a fast changing environment, it is quite possible that by the time the system is completed, the original requirements may have already become old fashioned. In addition, in the case of a small project, more time could be spent on planning and documentation than on designing, implementing and testing.
Thus, comprehensive testing is rarely finished. The step which is equivalent to quality checking for the product system cannot receive enough time to proceed. [2]
2.2 Testing in Incremental Model
In contrast with waterfall model, the incremental model has emerged in this rapidly changing environment. Methods of this model like Agile or XP usually use a test-driven development approach. In this approach, the whole project is broken down into several increments or iterations to be completed in shorter time boxes. In each iteration, tests are written before the actual implementation. An implementation is correct only if it can pass the existing test cases designed for it.
As a result, testing is interleaved with analysis, design, and implementation. So developers can spend more effective time on testing to have it carefully planned and carried out.
3.Principles of Testing
After having a good understanding of the importance of testing, this section discusses how general testing methods and techniques, i.e. static and dynamic methods, box testing, unit testing, integration testing, acceptance testing, etc., are applied in normal software development projects.
3.1 Test a program to try to make it fail
Dijkstra said that "testing shows the presence, not the absence of bugs [3]". The interpretation of this is obvious: except for trivial systems, those many test cases a developer can come up with are just a part of all possible scenarios. So testing is to execute the program with the intention to find bugs [4], not with the intention to show it is bug free. A good testing practice should show the program fails at some point, and after debugging, it can show the program successes at the same point.
3.2 Test early and regularly
Not surprising at all, fixing bugs is more expensive if it spotted at a later stage, but it is surprising how tremendously more expensive it is. Figure 1 shows that, in a waterfall model, cost of finding and fixing bugs is the result of an exponential function of time. It is also the case in test-driven approach, where a bug in an early iteration can accumulate to become a bigger problem and propagate to other components.
Figure 1. Cost of Fixing Bugs in Warterfall Model [5]
Additionally, tests should be carried out on a regular basis since when new components are added in, they may have unexpected effects on existing ones. Also, as long as the requirements are changed, test cases should be updated accordingly.
3.3 Testing is context dependant
The test methods to be used should depend on the context of the system to satisfy various requirements [6]. Test cases should be composed according to different components. Even with the same component in the same system, testing objectives can be different at different point of time. For example, unit testing checks if each component functions properly as individuals, while integration testing focuses on interaction between several components as a whole.
3.4 Define a Test Plan
A test plan should address test scope, test strategy, test methods and techniques, test results interpretation, and how comprehensive the test cases are to cover the possible scenarios. Also importantly, it should include how the tests are going to reveal the customer requirements, and how requirements are measured [7][8][9]. Furthermore, a risk assessment of the system under development should be considered here. The essence of risk assessment can be illustrated from the negative results of software disasters such as the Denver Airport Baggage Handling System [10] and the Fukoshima Nuclear Disaster [11]. Missing or under evaluating a risk may result in too few or even no specific tests covering this risk at all, which will further result in hidden faults, which finally leads to system failure.
3.5 Test for valid as well as invalid inputs
Test cases should of course include valid inputs, thus to mimic regular scenarios, which are the most likely real life situations. After those, developers should think about if things can go wrong with invalid inputs such as null pointers, out-of-bound index, etc. The reason is not only because statistically there are always a chance for exceptions to occur, but it is also quite often that a system is crashed by a single component which has got an unexpected input. Moreover, an interesting thing is, during testing, invalid input conditions seem to have higher error detection yield than test cases with valid input conditions [4].
4.Limitations of Testing
4.1 Testing cannot show bug-free
Also according to that famous quote of Dijkstra: "Testing shows the presence, not the absence of bugs [3]." In reality, testing is based on comparing actual outputs to expected outputs of a component in response to some inputs. These inputs are just a subset of all possible scenarios. Since very likely there are a great many of possibilities, it is rarely practical for one to be able to carry out exhaust testing. Hence, a good test case may indicate the existence of a fault within some component, or after the fault is corrected, it may show that component does not produce a particular kind of error when it receives a particular kind of input, but it never gives the idea that this component does not produce any kind of bug in response to any kind of input.
4.2 Tests are no substitute for specifications
With test-driven methods, developers write codes to pass the tests. Conventionally, the code becomes deliverable once it passes all tests. So to some extent, testing has substituted the requirement specification. However, tests, no matter how many test cases they include, are just instances of the requirements, which provide an abstraction of the expected outcome [12]. It is true that requirement specification is used for generating test cases, but inversely, using test cases to summarise a requirement is a conduct should be avoided. It is like a universal statement can be used to prove as many existential statements with the same predicate as desired, but no matter how many existential statements conjunction together, they cannot be used to prove a single universal statement with the same predicate.
4.3 Software testing does not help in finding root causes
IEEE standard terminology states:
"An unsatisfactory program execution is a 'failure', pointing to a 'fault' in the program, itself is the result of a 'mistake' in the programmer‚Äôs thinking."
According to section 3.1, testing is to execute the program to make it fail. It is the process to uncover failures in the program. So testing tells the developers the test subject does not generate satisfactory output in response to some certain inputs. However, it does not tell how the inputs are processed to result in such outputs. In other words, testing does not help in finding root causes, i.e. where, when, and how things go wrong, which lead the software to malfunction in the first place. That is done via another distinct activity known as debugging.
4.4 Extra Coding and Extra Chance to Have Bugs
No matter how automated the testing procedure a project is using, it requires some minimal level of human coding in the first place. Obviously, coding for testing means extra work to do. From instantiating components and initialising test inputs, to inter-component communication and results interpretationÔºå every piece of work is an additional programming task. Moreover, additional programming means additional chance to have bugs. For a failed test case, a developer has to check both the source code and test code for faults, because it may turn out to be that the logic or result interpretation is wrong within the test code.
5.Recommendation
Let us examine the definition in section 1 given by Kaner again. It is true that passing tests can at least show the software does not produce faulty outputs in situations covered by existing test cases. Plus, if these test cases are carefully planned, then it is reasonable for the stakeholders to be confident in the software's correctness. So the connection between testing and quality does exist and is important to keep in mind.
However, passing tests is equivalent to quality assurance for the product system is usually not the case. Test cases are instances of real life situations. They are elements of a subset of all possible inputs. What testing can prove is merely the performance based on that subset. Using the property of a subset to draw a conclusion for the full set is absolutely invalid.
6.References
[1] Kaner, C, 2006, Exploratory Testing, Key Note at QAI
http://www.kaner.com/pdfs/ETatQAI.pdf
[2] Sommerville, I, 2011, Software Engineering, 9th Edition, Pearson, Boston
[3] Dijkstra J.N. Buxton and B. Randell, eds, Software Engineering Techniques, April 1970, p. 16. Report on a conference sponsored by the NATO Science Committee, Rome, Italy, 27‚Äì31 October 1969.
http://homepages.cs.ncl.ac.uk/brian.randell/NATO/nato1969.PDF
[4] Myers, Glenford J., ‚ÄïThe art of software testing‚Äñ, New York: Wiley, c1979. ISBN: 0471043281
[5] Software Testing‚ÄìGoals, Principles, and Limitations
http://www.ijcaonline.org/volume6/number9/pxc3871448.pdf
[6] Shari Lawrence Pfleeger, "Software Engineering, Theory
and Practice", Pearson Education, 2001.
[7] James Whittaker, The 10 Minute Test Plan, Google Testing Blog
http://googletesting.blogspot.com.au/2011/09/10-minute-test-plan.html
[8] Test Plan, Wikipedia
http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Test_plan

http://www.wikihow.com/Write-a-Test-Plan

Adding Prac5 (resubmission)
https://github.com/gardners/2014SE3/issues/250
Unsolved
Introduction
This practical will supply a comprehensive test plan for the game 2048. The main objective of test plan is examine the program behavior and accuracy. The functioning of the game is to tilt the gaming board (4X4 grid) to move the tiles containing values floating on the board in the left, right, top and bottom direction. The objective of the game is to merge the two tiles containing the same values and the resulting tile will represent the summation of two equal values. After merging two tiles a tilt of the gaming board in any direction will generate a new tile with the multiple value of 2, 4, 16 e.g. The ultimate goal of the game is to achieve a tile containing the value 2048. The score will be increased with the value equal to the value produced with the merging of two identical tiles. At the beginning of the game two tiles containing either 2 or 4 will be appeared in two random locations of the gaming board. The score will be initialized as zero at the beginning of the game. The game will be considered to be over while there is no empty cell left to move any of the tiles on the board and while the player achieved the tile containing value 2048.
Software Specifications
i. NetBeans IDE version 8
ii. Github account algh0065
iii. Internet connection
Test Scenarios
Game Board Representation
At the initial stage of the game a test is performed to check the representation of the board. The test is performed for game board representation as follows:
i. A 4X4 grid will represent the entire board of the game, where two tiles will be highlighted at random locations of the board in the beginning.
ii. The highlighted two tiles will contain 2 values individually.
Substantiation of User Input
In order to verify the user input the following test steps are performed.
i. The input is considered to be valid if the user chooses any of the keyboard buttons namely 1, 2, 3, 4, or x.
ii. The input is considered to be invalid if the use chooses any other buttons other than 1, 2, 3, 4 or x.
iii. An invalid input resulting in error message pop-up saying that invalid input.
Conducting User Input
This will test the movements of the board while pressing particular input button.
i. The game board must be tilted up for the input of ‚Äò1‚Äô button of the keyboard.
ii. The game board must be tilted down for the input of ‚Äò2‚Äô button of the keyboard.
iii. The game board must be tilted right for the input of ‚Äò3‚Äô button of the keyboard.
iv. The game board must be tilted left for the input of ‚Äò4‚Äô button of the keyboard.
Tilting in the Up Direction
This will test the conditions for which the tiles will move up.
i. Tiles must move to the up when there are empty cells in the above of the columns of current tiles position.
ii. One Tile must move to the up and merge a tile of the same value in the above of the current tile value.
iii. A Tile must not move to the up when there is no empty cell in the above of the column of the current tile position.
iv. Tiles must not move to the up when they reached the top most position (i.e., top edge) of the board.
Tilting in the Down Direction
This will test the conditions for which the tiles will move down.
i. Tiles must move to the down when there are empty cells in the below of the columns of current tiles position.
ii. One Tile must move to the down and merge a tile of the same value in the below of the current tile value.
iii. A Tile must not move to the down when there is no empty cell in the below of the column of the current tile position.
iv. Tiles must not move to the down when they reached the bottom most position (i.e., bottom edge) of the board.
Tilting in the Right Direction
This will test the conditions for which the tiles will move right.
i. Tiles must move to the right when there are empty cells in the right of the rows of current tiles position.
ii. One Tile must move to the right and merge a tile of the same value in the right of the current tile value.
iii. A Tile must not move to the right when there is no empty cell in the right of the row of the current tile position.
iv. Tiles must not move to the right when they reached the right most position (i.e., right edge) of the board.
Tilting in the Left Direction
This will test the conditions for which the tiles will move left.
i. Tiles must move to the left when there are empty cells in the left of the rows of current tiles position.
ii. One Tile must move to the left and merge a tile of the same value in the left of the current tile value.
iii. A Tile must not move to the left when there is no empty cell in the left of the row of the current tile position.
iv. Tiles must not move to the left when they reached the left most position (i.e., left edge) of the board.
Condition for Merging Two Tiles
This will illustrate the condition for which two tiles will be merged into one.
i. Merging is possible to get one tile with the addition of the values containing two tiles only when the two tiles containing the same value and positioned adjacent to each other.
Score Calculation
The score of the game will be calculated in the following ways:
ii. At the very beginning of the game the score will be initialized as zero.
iii. The score will be increased with the value equal to the value obtained through merging of two tiles of equal values.
Game Expiration (Game Over)
The game will be expired in the following conditions:
i. The user may terminate the game anytime during the game by pressing the ‚Äòx‚Äô button.
ii. The game will be terminated when the user achieved the desired value 2048 in one tile and a message will pop-up representing game over.
iii. The game will be terminated when there is no empty cell left to move any of the tiles in any direction and a message will pop-up representing game over.
Game Limitations
The limitations of the game is pointed in the following
i. There is no option for this game kept for multi-user at a time.
ii. There are no multiple levels maintained for this game.
iii. Since it is a single player game the networking option is invalid.
Dependencies and Risks
There are some dependencies and risks reflected with this game. It is recommended that the user should learn the functioning and the rules of the game in order to be able to avoid risks for playing the game.

The problem is fixed by adding auth info:
java -jar jenkins-cli.jar -s http://localhost:8080/ list-plugins --username admin --password PASSWORD

.gitignore pattern ambigous
https://github.com/Stvad/Software_Engineering__git/issues/1
Unsolved
The question
What .gitignore pattern would you use to ignore all .txt files in the doc folder?
is ambigous with it asking for
doc/**/*.txt
because
doc/*.txt
is the right one according to the minimum information principle. The correct question would be
What .gitignore pattern would you use to ignore all .txt files under the doc folder?
, as the in is the most fitting word to describe files only directly in the doc folder, but not any subfolders. I know this is just a slight difference and subject to personal preferences, but we should be able to declare it too ambiguous and therefore subject to result in different thoughtpaths on each revising and we know this results in poor learning efficiency.
namibj opened this issue on 8 Oct 2016 ¬∑ 2 comments

Referencing to papers and/or software via stable links where possible
https://github.com/slebok/slebok/issues/23
Unsolved
I propose to reference any external artifact through generic, well-accepted links, with some confidence of stability. This includes DOIs (dx.doi...), links to institutional repositories (INRIA Hal, CWI repo, etc.), Wikipedia or Archive (if we must).
This would, however, exclude: homepages, blogs, and bibsleigh or related projects (in order to minimize dependencies on "third"-party projects ;-).

Attribute grammar terms

Unsolved
Overall plan:
Add AG terms into the glossary of terms (mostly G√∂rel)
Synchronize with the AG reader (Tony, Eric, ...)
Internal review by AG people (Tony, Eric, PhD students in our groups, ...)
Review by non-AG people (Benoit, Tanya, ...)
Guidelines:
Most of the terms have the word attribute in the filename.
All the terms should be reachable from the main entry: attribute_grammar.md
Terms left to write about:
concurrent attribute evaluation
object-oriented attribute grammars
attribute evaluation during parsing (like in ANTLR)
context conditions
abstract grammar
extending AGs with relations

SLE reader
https://github.com/slebok/slebok/issues/12
Unsolved
I really like the idea expressed by @inkytonik during the round of introductions, about creating the SLE reader by boldly going everywhere, including where no man has gone before. In other words, to have a reasonably comprehensive list/tree of overview papers, each of which classified into one of the three categories:
nice/ready/complete - where we are completely happy with the overview and can use it in SLE courses as is
imperfect/biased - where a good overview exists (such as Grune-Jacobs' Parsing Techniques or Sebesta's Concepts), but it id not SLE-able enough to be immediatelt useful in our context
nonexistant/could-be/would-be - where an overview is totally possible and conceivable, but not written yet. Hopefully having a well-defined request like this will inspire people (especially young researchers who have a lot of time on their hands and want to get famous) to write those.
grammarware opened this issue on 23 Aug 2017 ¬∑ 2 comments

Glossary/Terms: Decide on format
https://github.com/slebok/slebok/issues/9
Unsolved
The current recommendation is in Template4C&P.md
Most entries are imported from Anya's glossary and not totally integrated with this yet
Anya's imports look like this:
Entry name (abbreviation
Also known as / Related to
other relevant terms
Definition
Links
[Wikipedia]
Tags
Types, Semantics, Languages
The current Template looks like this:
Entry Template for C&P (Term goes here)
Definition
(definition goes here)
(commentary, or link to other sources)
Disambiguation
(may not apply)
Classification
superterm > superterm > (this term)
First Mention
(some DBLP references here, or references into BibSLEIGH)
Known Instances
(list of known instances here; may not apply)

Added BDD feature management / Basic PDF export
https://github.com/tmerten/redmine_re/pull/3
Unsolved
Hi There,
First thanks for your great work. It helped me to increase the productivity of my customer and to tighten the requirements definition process and management as well. Basically what the KOREM plugin was intended for.
As I suggested my customer to select a Behavior Driven Development (BDD) approach for their projects to collect requirements I added the possibility to KOREM to add so called features from the BDD philosophy to the Redmine database. For further information on this please read on here.
One missing feature also was that it is not simply possible to export the requirements and other added data from the plugin. We could have done this via an external interface (e.g. database admin interface), but a direct export was mandatory.
So I spend the effort and also added the possibility to export the tree structure as flat PDF file by right clicking on the tree root node and select the "Export" option. This feature uses pdfkit which requires wkhtmltopdf - I updated the gem file accordingly and added some information to the README.rdoc file.
I would be happy if you merge the changes in your main stream and if we could get together to talk about further adjustments which I have in mind, not only related to the export function, but also to other missing features.
Cheers,
Marvin Kruse
Philotech GmbH

Feature todo api server
https://github.com/ZEPL/data-engineering-challenge/pull/8
Unsolved
How to run test
./gradlew test
How to run
./gradlew run
or
./gradlew fatJar
java -jar build/libs/todo-all-1.0-SNAPSHOT.jar 8000
Design Decisions/Thinking
Not used mock because it's simple
time vs string for created field - There's no date manipulation, so I'll use String
Intentionally less comments - Try to write self-explained code
Split Todo/Task of Dao, Service, Resource? I choose not to split because Task actions are always with todoId.
When empty result - 200 vs 204? I think it's better to reply 204 than return empty result such as [], but it's okay to return 200.
Very basic storage model - store whole data in one file
Simple cmdline args processing
Guice + Jersey2 is not that fun to work with together...:(
What I didn't do because of it's not necessary or there's not enough time
Concurrency - I only apply locking for saving to file of the data. There're many issues such as Lost Updates, Inconsistent Retrievals, etc. To prevent them, transactional processing mechanism is required.
A thorough param check, logging, exception handling.
Usually, I prefer to write each layers of Resource, Service, DAO, etc independently with mocking, but pass this time.
Real DB with JPA - I think the requirements showed that real DB/JPA is not necessary.
Deploying to server
ghost wants to merge 25 commits into ZEPL:master
from unknown repository

todo-challenge solution
https://github.com/ZEPL/data-engineering-challenge/pull/7
Unsolved
Todo Challenge Solution
Build and Run
$ mvn compile
$ mvn exec:java -Dexec.mainClass=dhrim.zeplchallenge.todo.Main -Dexec.args="-p 8080"
TestCase
mvn test
3 test case exist.
TodoRestApiTest : call REST api by http request. It use mock Repo instead of real Repo.
IntegrationTest : test with real Repo.
MapDbTodoRepoTest : test working with MapDb.
Architecture
Resource --> Service --> Repo
TodoRestApi : Jersey resource file. endpoint is defined. call TodoService
TodoService : treat business logic. use TodoRepo for storing
TodoRepo : repository interface
-- AbstractMapBaseTodoRepo : abstract repo class which use map
-- MapDbTodoRepo : concret repo class which extends AbstractMapBaseTodoRepo.
TodoServer : Server Main. provide getInstance() which create instance by Guice
Repository
Use MapDb(http://www.mapdb.org/) for storing which use local file for persistence.
Limitation
Didn't consider expandability. It means only valid for single server beacuse of repository
Didn't consider performance
Didn't treat detail exception case. Not defined in requirement as like duplicated name.
Change Endpoint
GET /todos/:todo_id for get task list is not correct.
I implemented with GET /todos/:todl_id/tasks instead.

Design issue in association class section
https://github.com/se-edu/se-book/issues/45
Unsolved
Hi there! I was looking through your online book, and I wanted to point out that there's a design issue in the section on inheritance. From the text:
However, the two classes cannot be simply replaced with a more general class Person because of the need to distinguish between Man and Woman for the ‚Äòmarriage‚Äô association. A solution is to add the Person class as a super class and let Man and Woman inherit from Person.
Given that same-sex marriage is legal in most of the developed world, distinguishing between Man and Woman in the class Marriage makes the implementation fragile to changes in requirements. A more robust solution is to use the type Person.
This is actually a really good example of how untested assumptions that we as software engineers make can come back to haunt us later. This could be a good object lesson on the need for requirements analysis.
rmmilewi opened this issue on 8 May ¬∑ 1 comment


None
Unsolved



Questions: Remove duplication from answers
https://github.com/se-edu/se-book/issues/40
Unsolved
The answer can contain just the a, b, c etc. like so:
<panel header=":lock::key: What are the advantages of using use cases (the textual form) for requirements modelling?">
<question>

What are the advantages of using use cases (the textual form) for requirements modelling?

- [ ] a. They can be fairly detailed but still natural enough for users for users to understand and give feedback.
- [ ] b. The UI-independent nature of use case specification allows the system designers more freedom to decide how a functionality is provided to a user.
- [ ] c. Extensions encourage us to consider all situations a software product might face during its operations.
- [ ] d. They encourage us to identify and optimize the typical scenario of usage over exceptional usage scenarios.
- [ ] e. All of the above.
- [ ] f. First three only.

<div slot="answer">

e

</div>
</question>
</panel>

Full-time or permanent employees?
https://github.com/triketora/women-in-software-eng/issues/283
Solved
In the contributing doc, it states:
Only full-timers please; no interns or contractors.
Does this actually mean full-timers, or does it mean 'permanent employees'?
We have contractors who are full-time, but some of our most senior engineers are permanent employees who are a core part of our engineering team, but work four days a week, so wouldn't qualify as full-timers. It would feel very strange not to include them in our numbers.

Data Free To Use?
https://github.com/triketora/women-in-software-eng/issues/75
Solved
Is the data presented in this project free for others to use (non-commercially of course)?
I'm a Software Engineer at Webkite. We develop an application that takes raw data (typically from a CSV file) and builds a searchable website which we refer to as a "Kite".
After @gregates submitted his pull request with our numbers we discussed building a Kite from this data and making it public for everyone. To avoid any problems I figured we should ask before building anything.
Here's a basic example of one of our sites: http://netrunner.flyasite.com/.
Thoughts?
binarycleric opened this issue on 9 Nov 2013 ¬∑ 1 comment

Let's make this more than binary
https://github.com/triketora/women-in-software-eng/issues/3
Solved
I'd like this amazing idea to benefit from more than just women:men identities - let's broaden and allow for people to self-id in other categories then analyze the data accordingly.
eg: instead of pulling num_female_eng and num_eng let's say grab num* and chart that so a company could have (and people could make pull requests for data that looks like):
[company_name]
company: Name
num_women_eng: 13
num_men_eng: 92
num_transwoman_eng: 2
num_genderqueer_eng: 1
last_updated: 10/20/2013
Then sort this based on whatever is between num_ and _eng to get the columns or whatever.
I could submit a patch for this probably but putting it in an issue in case anyone else wants to tackle this before I get to it. Thanks for doing this!
lsblakk opened this issue on 22 Oct 2013 ¬∑ 11 comments

Distinguish between deleted and emptied files in diff shield
https://github.com/phacility/phabricator/pull/842
Solved
The Phabricator UI uses a rendershield over file contents when the content in various contexts, including when the file is empty. In empty cases, it currently uses the text "This file was completely deleted.", even when the file is still present, but empty.
This change addresses that issue by checking if the underlying file was deleted (or simply modified), and showing the text "This file was completely emptied." in the edge case.

Improve password reset message
https://github.com/phacility/phabricator/pull/831
Solved
The existing password reset message gives terrible advice, in what I think was probably an attempt at sarcasm. Unfortunately sarcasm is often lost on many users and this messaging will at best end up being confusing and create more work for teams that support phabricator.
I'm proposing new default language that keeps the spirit of the original but with better security advice without any sarcasm that could lead to confusion or more work for teams supporting phabricator.

Status Closed should also concieved as Accepted
https://github.com/phacility/phabricator/pull/828
Solved
This is related to a scenarion in https://secure.phabricator.com/T4754.
arc feature
... do work ...
arc diff
(Diff accepted)
arc land
(Herald rule checks status == accepted, allows commit)
(Commit worker detects diff and closes it)
git checkout lts
git cherry-pick master
git push ....
(Herald rule sees status == closed, rejects push) (this should be allowed)

user/{userId} include ownUser boolean
https://github.com/SoftwareEngineeringDaily/software-engineering-daily-api/issues/156
Solved
Working on the front-end to add public profile for any user. I'd like to conditionally display an "Edit Profile" link if it's the authenticated user's own user being viewed.
Given the current front-end, I'd need to make a call to user/{userId} and user/me which is not a huge issue, but an unnecessary api call.
There are two alternative options here as far as I can tell:
Change front-end to fetch "me" profile as soon as logging on
Include an ownUser boolean to GET user/{userId} to back-end
Further alternate ideas are welcome. This might be a good first issue if agreed to.
joshmorel opened this issue on 3 Feb ¬∑ 3 comments

get user/:userId exposes user info that should be hidden
https://github.com/SoftwareEngineeringDaily/software-engineering-daily-api/issues/70
Solved
This wasn't a problem previously, because /users wasn't used in index.route.js. But now that it is, a call to api/users/:userId will return all user info even if you're not that same user or even logged in.
Something that might address this as well as support issues #36 and #56 going forward, could be a toAuthJSON and toProfileJSON functions which would only expose those elements to the same authenticated user and to anyone respectively. Here is a similar example.
Because there is both auth and user controller it seems it would be easiest to put in model but its worth discussing.
As a stop gap - simply disabling the route might be the best choice (my guess is it isn't used anywhere, because the /users was only recently exposed)

Intended use of favorite vs upvote/downvote
https://github.com/SoftwareEngineeringDaily/software-engineering-daily-api/issues/60
Solved
What's the intended use of favoriting vs upvote/downvote?
I see the use of upvote/downvote as similar to youtube which makes sense. Why also have favoriting? From my perspective, you would have one function or the other in an app, but not both.
Similar but perhaps semantically more meaningful might be "bookmark", which could be used if you want to keep as a list eps to listen to later, eps you might like to listen to again/do more research on related resources. Upvote/downvote would be intended only for those you've listened to (or partially listened to) already.

https://github.com/j-delaney/easy-application/issues/142
Solved
Hello, I wrote a tool that can validate README links. It can be run when someone submits a pull request.
For example, you would see that
https://jobs.lever.co/pristine/ is now 404
http://www.cloudera.com/about-cloudera/careers.html redirects to http://jobs.jobvite.com/cloudera/
There are actually 92 redirects and 14 dead links https://gist.github.com/5d42a9246fcb7d0b28866bc415e7311f
This tool is currently being used by
https://github.com/matteocrippa/awesome-swift
https://github.com/brabadu/awesome-fonts
and many more
Examples
https://travis-ci.org/matteocrippa/awesome-swift/builds/96526196 ok ‚úÖ
https://travis-ci.org/matteocrippa/awesome-swift/builds/96722421 link redirected / rename üî¥
https://travis-ci.org/dkhamsing/open-source-ios-apps/builds/96763135 bad link / project deleted üî¥
https://travis-ci.org/dkhamsing/open-source-ios-apps/builds/95754715 dupe üî¥
If you are interested, connect this repo to https://travis-ci.org/ and add a .travis.yml file to the project (you can also use Circle CI or other CI services).
See https://github.com/dkhamsing/awesome_bot for options, more information

cloudera is not an easy application
https://github.com/j-delaney/easy-application/issues/118
Solved
Cloudera should be removed from this repository because their application form is long and because the tos are unfriendly to job seekers.
Cloudera's application is long. It is a multi-step form that requires the applicant to manually fill in data about previous employers and school background.
Cloudera's tos are unfriendly to job seekers. Cloudera's tos include an NDA, which job seekers must agree to before submitting their application. The application obfuscates the fact that applicants are submitting to an NDA in two ways. First, the next button scrolls down automatically so the applicant does not see NDA in the title "Cloudera Employment Application and NDA". Second, the application combines this NDA as part of another form possibly making it unclear to applicants that they are submitting to an NDA.

Error linking with -Wl,--as-needed
https://github.com/thorkill/eresi/issues/146
Solved
On Gentoo with LDFLAGS=-Wl,--as-needed, eresi fails to link. The cause seems to be a bad library order in the e2dbg Makefile; some libraries listed there require symbols from stderesi in turn.
I wrote a [http://overlays.gentoo.org/proj/sunrise/browser/sunrise/dev-util/eresi/files/0.82_beta2-as-needed.patch patch] to fix this. You are welcome to incorporate it into your SVN, although I'd appreciate if the commit message would credit me.
Ticket: 139 Reported by: gagern on Mon Jul 5 16:54:27 2010
thorkill opened this issue on 24 Apr 2016 ¬∑ 0 comments

Cleanup call/ret/branch tags
https://github.com/thorkill/eresi/issues/145
Solved
Add three new tags INDCONTROL, CONDCONTROL and BRANCH to indicate indirect access, conditional execution and branch instruction to libasm's flags list.
Change uses of CONDBRANCH and IMPBRANCH to a combination of these three flags.

x86 shortjump has wrong operand type
https://github.com/thorkill/eresi/issues/139
Solved
Short jumps should have an operand type of ASM_OTYPE_SHORTJUMP, but end up with ASM_OTYPE_JUMP instead. asm_operand_fetch_shortjump does receive otype == ASM_OTYPE_SHORTJUMP, but ignores it and assigns ASM_OTYPE_JUMP. Patch attached. (I'm not sure why the operand handlers all receive otype, only to ignore it.)
Ticket: 132 Reported by: glenn on Sun Mar 21 06:43:33 2010
attachment: fix-shortjump-operand.diff/
thorkill opened this issue on 24 Apr 2016 ¬∑ 0 comments

trivial header breakage in c++
https://github.com/thorkill/eresi/issues/138
Solved
The headers work in C++ except for one thing: enum asm_instr in libasm/include/libasm-i386.h conflicts with the struct of the same name.
This enum never seems to be used by name, so renaming it is simple.

libmjollnir CFG error
https://github.com/thorkill/eresi/issues/133
Solved
there is an error in libmjollnir CFG module, in links.c mjr_link_block_jump function, the src block might be spited, this is not considered, so if the source and destination are in the same bloc, after the spit, the source block should be recalculated.
here is an example
suppose before the mjr_link_block_jump function, we have a basic block
1
2
3
4
and the parameter for mjr_link_block_jump is source is 4 , dst is 2 , ret is 5
so in the function, we first get the block associated with src, which starts at 1, after the spit we have two block 1 and 2 3 4
and the links added is [1] -> [2, 3, 4] [1] -> [5] which are wrong,
we need to recalculate the source block, which is [2,3,4] and the right links should be [2, 3, 4] -> [2, 3,4] and [2,3,4] -> [5].

elfsh_register_* assumes that sizeof(int) == sizeofvoid *)
https://github.com/thorkill/eresi/issues/132
Solved
The various elfsh_register_* functions cast a pointer to an int, but on amd64 sizeof(int) < sizeof(void *) so this will break.
The attached patch corrects the casts.

Solved

"Git miscellany" page
https://github.com/UCL/rsd-engineeringcourse/issues/75
Solved
In the git stash area of the page, it's not clear what is going on.
From the documentation:
"Use git stash when you want to record the current state of the working directory and the index, but want to go back to a clean working directory. The command saves your local modifications away and reverts the working directory to match the HEAD commit.
The modifications stashed away by this command can be listed with git stash list, inspected with git stash show, and restored (potentially on top of a different commit) with git stash apply. "
So in the example it looks like a local change is stashed, then the remote repo pulled, and finally the stash applied on top of that, but for new users this isn't clear.
In the Tagging section, the second half doesn't seem to have anything to do with tagging.
In Git clean section, ad brief note to explain what it does i.e. (from documentation) Remove untracked files from the working tree.
Yaml Frontmatter section. The linked page doesn't appear to explain anything.

GitHub Contributions on Profile Pages
https://github.com/SoftwareEngineeringDaily/sedaily-front-end/issues/480
Solved
I was working on getting GitHub contributions up on the profile page, should we create a specific vue.js npm package for this? I was originally thinking about importing an external script, and it seems to work fine, but for the purposes of maintaining for the future, it could be a little sloppy.
Here's a mock-up with this integration:
@joshmorel @dfcook @andrewmarklloyd @jasonify
mounted: function() {
      let gitHubCalenderScript = document.createElement('script')
      gitHubCalenderScript.setAttribute('src', 'https://cdn.rawgit.com/IonicaBizau/github-calendar/gh-pages/dist/github-calendar.min.js')
      gitHubCalenderScript.async = true
      document.head.appendChild(gitHubCalenderScript)

      GitHubCalendar(".calendar", userData.github, {responsive: true})
}
